#  Districting Process - 2016 
![Districts Header](https://www.anaheim.net/ImageRepository/Document?documentID=11399)
  1. [Overview](https://www.anaheim.net/5807/Districting-Process---2016#tabf495ed73-1740-48fc-b1d6-938c7450d2fe_0)
  2. [Boundaries](https://www.anaheim.net/5807/Districting-Process---2016#tabf495ed73-1740-48fc-b1d6-938c7450d2fe_1)
  3. [Districting Process](https://www.anaheim.net/5807/Districting-Process---2016#tabf495ed73-1740-48fc-b1d6-938c7450d2fe_2)
  4. [Meeting Minutes and Videos](https://www.anaheim.net/5807/Districting-Process---2016#tabf495ed73-1740-48fc-b1d6-938c7450d2fe_3)


  1. [Overview](https://www.anaheim.net/5807/Districting-Process---2016#tabf495ed73-1740-48fc-b1d6-938c7450d2fe_0)


For the first time in Anaheim’s 159 year history, Anaheim’s “At-Large” system for electing City Council Members changed to a “By-District” system with the mayor continuing to be elected At-Large. 
After months of community meetings and public hearings by the Advisory Committee and City Council, on February 9, 2016 the City Council unanimously adopted the city’s first districting map and election sequence for the six Council district seats.
[![District Map Opens in new window](https://www.anaheim.net/ImageRepository/Document?documentID=11360)](http://www.anaheim.net/DocumentCenter/View/11401/District-Map?bidId= "District Map") |  [![Final Report Opens in new window](https://www.anaheim.net/ImageRepository/Document?documentID=35524)](https://www.anaheim.net/ImageRepository/Document?documentId=9187 "Final Report") |  [![Census Data Opens in new window](https://www.anaheim.net/ImageRepository/Document?documentID=11361)](http://anaheim.net/DocumentCenter/View/11369/Census-Data?bidId= "Census Data")  
---|---|---  
  1. [Boundaries](https://www.anaheim.net/5807/Districting-Process---2016#tabf495ed73-1740-48fc-b1d6-938c7450d2fe_1)


Legal descriptions of the city council district boundaries are listed below. (Source: [Ordinance No. 6360](http://records.anaheim.net/CityClerk/DocView.aspx?dbid=0&id=1605697&page=1))  
  
**Council District 1** :   
All the land within the boundary beginning at the northwest corner of the intersection of Brookhurst Avenue and California Route 91 on the northern boundary of the City of Anaheim, proceeding southerly on Brookhurst Avenue to Crescent Avenue; then proceeding westerly on Crescent Avenue to Magnolia Avenue; then proceeding southerly on Magnolia Avenue to the southern boundary of the City of Anaheim; then proceeding westerly, northerly, and easterly on the boundary of the City of Anaheim to the point of origin.  
  
**Council District 2:**  
All the land within the boundary beginning at the northwest corner of the intersection of Brookhurst Avenue and California Route 91 on the northern boundary of the City of Anaheim, proceeding southerly on Brookhurst Avenue to Crescent Avenue; then proceeding westerly on Crescent Avenue to Magnolia Avenue; then proceeding southerly on Magnolia Avenue to the southern boundary of the City of Anaheim; then proceeding easterly on the southern boundary of the City of Anaheim to the intersection of Katella Avenue and Euclid Street; then proceeding northerly on Euclid Street to the intersection of Euclid Street and California Route 91, which is the city boundary; then proceeding westerly on the boundary of the City of Anaheim to the point of origin.  
  
**Council District 3:**  
All the land within the boundary beginning at the northwest corner of Raymond Avenue and the northern boundary of the City of Anaheim, proceeding southerly on Raymond Avenue, which becomes East Street, to South Street; then proceeding westerly on South Street to Interstate 5; then proceeding southerly on Interstate 5 to Ball Road; then proceeding westerly on Ball Road to Walnut Street; then proceeding northerly on Walnut Street to Crone Avenue; then proceeding westerly on Crone Avenue to Euclid Street; then proceeding northerly on Euclid Street to the intersection of Euclid Street and California Route 91, which is the city boundary; then proceeding easterly, northerly and then easterly on the boundary of the City of Anaheim to the point of origin.  
  
**Council District 4:**  
All the land within the boundary beginning at the northwest corner of the intersection of Orangewood Avenue and Anaheim Way on the southern boundary of the City of Anaheim, proceeding northerly on Anaheim Way to Lewis Street; then proceeding northerly on Lewis Street to Ball Road; then proceeding easterly on Ball Road to State College Boulevard; then proceeding northerly on State College Boulevard to Santa Ana Street; then proceeding westerly on Santa Ana Street to East Street; then proceeding southerly on East Street to South Street; then proceeding westerly on South Street to Interstate 5; then proceeding southerly on Interstate 5 to Ball Road; then proceeding westerly on Ball Road to Walnut Street; then proceeding northerly on Walnut Street to Crone Avenue; then proceeding westerly on Crone Avenue to Euclid Street; then proceeding southerly on Euclid Street to the intersection of Euclid Street and Katella Avenue, which is the city boundary; then proceeding easterly on the boundary of the City of Anaheim to the point of origin.  
  
**Council District 5:**  
All the land within the boundary beginning at the intersection of Orangethorpe Avenue and the northern boundary of the City of Anaheim, proceeding southwesterly on Orangethorpe Avenue to Miller Street; then proceeding southeasterly on Miller Street to La Palma Avenue; then proceeding southwesterly on La Palma Avenue to Kraemer Boulevard; then proceeding southeasterly on Kraemer Boulevard, which becomes Glassell Street, to the southern boundary of the City of Anaheim; then proceeding westerly on the southern boundary of the City of Anaheim to the intersection of Orangewood Avenue and Anaheim Way; then proceeding northerly on Anaheim Way to Lewis Street; then proceeding northerly on Lewis Street to Ball Road; then proceeding easterly on Ball Road to State College Boulevard; then proceeding northerly on State College Boulevard to Santa Ana Street; then proceeding westerly on Santa Ana Street to East Street; then proceeding northerly on East Street, which becomes Burton Avenue, to the boundary of the City of Anaheim; then proceeding easterly on the boundary of the City of Anaheim to the point of origin.  
  
**Council District 6:**  
All the land within the boundary beginning at the intersection of Orangethorpe Avenue and the northern boundary of the City of Anaheim, proceeding southwesterly on Orangethorpe Avenue to Miller Street; then proceeding southeasterly on Miller Street to La Palma Avenue; then proceeding southwesterly on La Palma Avenue to Kraemer Boulevard; then proceeding southeasterly on Kraemer Boulevard, which becomes Glassell Street, to the southern boundary of the City of Anaheim; then proceeding easterly, northerly, and westerly on the boundary of the City of Anaheim to the point of origin.   

  1. [Districting Process](https://www.anaheim.net/5807/Districting-Process---2016#tabf495ed73-1740-48fc-b1d6-938c7450d2fe_2)


On November 4, 2014 Anaheim voters approved [Measure L](http://www.anaheim.net/documentcenter/view/8991) and [Measure M](http://www.anaheim.net/documentcenter/view/8993). As such, at the Council meeting on April 7, 2015, the City Council appointed an Advisory Committee on Electoral Districts (“Committee”) to obtain input from Anaheim residents on the shape of the six City Council voting districts and to recommend a path forward. The Committee was selected by random draw from a panel of retired judges with a preference given to judges who reside within the City of Anaheim. The judges had served on the Orange County Superior Court and are residents of Orange County. The five selected judges served as volunteers.  
  
Following Committee appointment, the Committee immediately held 10 public meetings across Anaheim to ensure all residents were educated about the districting process and to promote participation and equal access to all meetings.   
  
The city's demographer, Justin Levitt, was present during each meeting to answer questions of the Committee and the public relating to his analysis of Anaheim's community based on current census data (2010). Among many things, he also provided hands-on assistance to members of the public who were interested in developing district boundary maps and submitting them to the Committee.  
  
After months of conducting public meetings, reviewing 39 maps, hearing public testimony from over 700 residents, and consulting with the City’s demographer, the Committee recommended [one map](http://anaheim.net/DocumentCenter/View/9186) to the Anaheim City Council.   
  
On October 6, 2015, the Committee submitted its [Final Report](http://anaheim.net/DocumentCenter/View/9187) and [Recommended Plan](http://anaheim.net/DocumentCenter/View/9186) to the City Council. The Recommended Plan places two city landmarks – the Anaheim Resort and Platinum Triangle – into two districts. It also has one Latino-majority CVAP and two Latino-plurality CVAP, as well as keeps communities of interests together.  
  
The Final Report was based on public testimony, federal and state laws and criteria set by the City Council. The U.S. Constitution requires districts contain roughly equal population and the Federal Voting Rights Act prohibit racial gerrymandering. In establishing the boundaries of the districts, the Committee and the City Council considered at least the following factors:   
  
• The U.S. Constitution  
• The Voting Rights Act of 1965  
• California Elections Code  
• District population equality  
• Topography and geography  
• Cohesiveness, contiguity, integrity and compactness of territory  
• Communities of interest  
• Future population growth
After receiving the [Final Report](http://anaheim.net/DocumentCenter/View/9187) of the Advisory Committee on Electoral Districts, the City Council held a series of public hearings to determine district boundaries for Anaheim’s six City Council voting districts, as well as which four City Council districts would hold elections in 2016 and which two would hold elections in 2018.  
  
On February 9, 2016, the City Council unanimously adopted the Recommended Plan (Map 3) to serve as the city’s first district boundary map. The City Council also set Districts 1, 3, 4, and 5 for the November 8, 2016 ballot. The remaining two districts (2 & 6) held elections in 2018.

Advisory Committee on Electoral Districts

Shape Anaheim’s Future Draw your City Council Districts. Page | 1

회의 안건 위원회 회원
* * *
## 년 5월 2 7일 수 요 일 Hon. Edward Wallin, Ret., 회장
오후 6:30 Hon. Stephen Sundvold, Ret., 부회장
* * *
Anaheim City Council Chambers Hon. James Jackman, Ret.
* * *
## _200 Anaheim Blvd., 1st Floor Anaheim 92805 Hon. Nancy Wieben Stock, Ret._
Hon. Thomas Thrasher, Ret.
* * *
1. 개회 선언
* * *
2. 공공 의견 (3분 – 모든 안건 항목)
* * *
3. 시의회 선거구역 및 규칙, 기준 설정
* * *
4. 자문위원회 회의 원격 개최지에 대한 승인
* * *
5. 5월 12일 자문위원회 회의 기록에 대한 승인
* * *
6. 위원회 의견 / 직원 의견
* * *
7. 폐회
* * *
***** 모든 안건과 보충 자료들은 시청 사무실 또는 http://www.anaheim.net/article.asp?id=5419에서 이용하실 수 있습니다. 이 안건과 관련된 (법률상 공표가 면제된 문서 이 외) 위원회 다수에게 제공된 모든 종류의 서면 또는 서류를 200 S. Anaheim Blvd., 2nd Floor, Anaheim, CA 92805에 위치한 시청 사무실에서 개방 시간 내에 이용하실 수 있습니다.
* * *
공개 회의 참여를 위해 보조 도움 또는 서비스를 포함한 장애 관련 수정 또는 시설이 필요한 개인은 관련된 수정 사항, 시설, 도움 또는 서비스를 예정된 회의일 1일전 오전 10:00시까지 200 South Anaheim Boulevard, Anaheim, California 에 위치한 시청 사무실로 연락 주시거나 (714) 765-5166 로 문의 주시면 됩니다. 요청 시, 1990 년 발효된 미국 장애인복지법 202 항에 따라, 장애를 가진 개인에게 적절한 대안의 조치가 이루어질 것입니다.
* * *
통역 서비스: 선거구 자문위원회 회의 내 스페인어 통역 서비스가 제공됩니다. 헤드셋 사용을 통해 스페인어 동시 통역 서비스가 제공되며 의회에 요청을 해주시면 순차 통역 (스페인어-영어) 서비스도 누구나 이용하실 수 있습니다. 시에서 제공하는 통역사 사용은 필수 사항이 아니며 개인 통역사 서비스를 이용하셔도 됩니다. 많은 방언과 지역주의가 존재하기 때문에 시에서는 해당 통역사가 특정 단어 또는 지역주의에 맞게 통역을 할 것인지의 여부에 대해 보장하지 않으며, 이러한 서비스로 인해 일어날 수 있는 모든 법적 책임을 지지 않습니다. 다른 언어의 통역 서비스를 원하시는 경우, 회의 일정 이전 48 시간 전에 시청 사무실로 연락해주시기 바랍니다.
* * *
성명 게시: 2015 년 5 월 22 일, 이 안건의 최종안이 200 S. Anaheim Blvd.에 위치한 시청 바깥의 키오스크에 게시됨.
* * *
## RULES AND CRITERIA
**FOR DISTRICTING**
1 ITEM NO. 03
* * *
MEASURE L • Voters approved Charter amendment by 68.8% at the November, 2014 election. • Requires Council Members elected in 2016 and thereafter to live in and be elected from a geographic district, only by voters of that district. • Only one Council Member will be elected from each district. • Mayor remains elected at large. • Does not cut short any Council member's current term of office, or require residency in a district during current term
* * *
## MEASURE L – CON’T
• City Council is ultimately responsible for approving the districts and may not delegate this responsibility:! Districts must comply with state and federal law (discussed later)! City Council must also establish a transition plan to account for election to newly created seats and identify seats up for election in 2016 and 2018
* * *
MEASURE M • Voters approved Charter amendment by 54.2% at the November, 2014 election • Increases City Council members from four to six (plus Mayor) • Increase occurs at the November 2016 election:! Two existing Council seats that would already be on the ballot plus two newly created seats will be on the ballot, all four of which will be elected by district.! Following November 2016 election, one of the four elected will be randomly selected to serve a shorter 2 year term. The remaining three will serve 4 year terms.
* * *
LEGAL AUTHORITY U.S. Constitution Federal Statutory and Case Law California Elections Code Charter
* * *
FEDERAL RULES US Constitution: Equal Population among Districts As stated in Elections Code Section 21620 “the districts shall be as nearly equal in population as may be according to the latest federal decennial census” • Total population: not voting age population, citizens, or voters • No racial gerrymandering Federal Law: The Federal Voting Rights Act Section 2 – Ensure equal power to elect candidates of choice.
* * *
U.S. CONSTITUTION Equality of Population • The Equal Protection Clause of the 14th Amendment of the U.S. Constitution prohibits the election of local government officials from districts of disparate population. Avery v. Midland County, 390 U.S. 474 (1968) • Districts must be “as nearly equal in population as may be.” Id. • A total population deviation of 10% between largest and smallest legislative district is presumed to be acceptable. Gaffney v. Cummings, 412 U.S. 735 (1973); White v. Regester, 412 U.S. 755 (1973)
* * *
RACIAL GERRYMANDERING The Supreme Court has held that race may be considered as evidence of a community of interest, but may not be the predominant consideration absent highly unusual circumstances. Shaw v. Reno, 509 U.S. 630 (1993)
* * *
## Section 2 (42 U.S.C. § 1973)
No voting qualification or prerequisite to voting or standard, practice, or procedure shall be imposed or applied by any State or political subdivision in a manner which results in a denial or abridgement of the right of any citizen of the United States to vote on account of race or color, or in contravention of the guarantees set forth in (42 USC 1973b(f)(2) [language minorities, e.g. Hispanics]) … FEDERAL VOTING RIGHTS ACT
* * *
## Thornburg v. Gingles, 478 U.S. 30 (1986)
Although courts ultimately apply a totality of the circumstances test, a plaintiff bringing a claim under Section 2 must first establish the three Gingles threshold preconditions:
* * *
> “First, the minority group must be able to demonstrate that it
is sufficiently large and geographically compact to constitute a majority in a single-member district....
* * *
> “Second, the minority group must be able to show that it is
politically cohesive....
* * *
> “Third, the minority must be able to demonstrate that the
white majority votes sufficiently as a bloc to enable it... to defeat the minority’s preferred candidate.” FEDERAL VOTING RIGHTS ACT
* * *
## Bartlett v. Strickland, 129 S.Ct. 1231 (2009)
FEDERAL VOTING RIGHTS ACT While a minority Influence district may be created, the Act does not require it:
* * *
> “It remains the rule, however, that a party asserting § 2 liability
must show by a preponderance of the evidence that the minority population in the potential election district is greater than 50 percent…Our holding does not apply to cases in which there is intentional discrimination against a racial minority.”
* * *
Garza v. County of L.A.918 F. 2d 763 (1990) Intent to deprive minority group of voting rights violates the VRA even if the first Gingles precondition is not met, even if intent is not due to racial animus.
* * *
## Federal Voting Rights Act
Alabama Legislative Black Caucus v. Alabama, 575 U.S. ___ (2015) • Equality of population is primary, not just another criteria • Setting a predetermined arbitrary supermajority percentage of one group in a district raises Constitutional concerns. • The appropriate consideration is to preserve the minority group’s ability to elect its preferred candidate of choice.
* * *
## STATE RULES – CRITERIA
California Elections Code, Section 21620: • Equal population • In establishing the boundaries of the districts the Council may give consideration to the following factors: (a) Topography, (b) Geography, (c) Cohesiveness, contiguity, integrity, and compactness of territory, and (d) Community of interests of the districts.
* * *
## CRITERIA – CON’T
Reasons identified and approved by the US Supreme Court as justifiable reasons for small population deviations: Hunt v. Cromartie, 121 S.Ct. 1452 (2001) • Communities of interest • Follow Visible (natural & man-made) boundaries (e.g. rivers, streets) • Compactness and contiguity • Population growth • Providing voters the opportunity to retain their elected representatives, if they choose
* * *
## The goal is the creation of legislative districts
that are effective, both for the represented and the representative. DeWitt v. Wilson, 856 F. Supp. 1409 (1994) OUTCOME
* * *
## • Social and economic interests common to the
population of an area • Interests in common to an urban area, rural area, industrial area, agricultural area. • Interests in common to areas of similar living standards, transportation facilities, work opportunities, same media market relevant to the election process • Political subdivisions (e.g. school or special districts) COMMUNITIES OF INTEREST
* * *
Equal Population Based on total population US Census 2010 Data Goal: exact equality 10% deviation may be permissible Other data sources §2 Voting Rights Act Protects Voting/Voters Based on Citizen Voting Age Population from American Community Survey & DOJ Special Tabulation 2009-2013 DATA TO BE USED
* * *

City Demographics • 74.5% have a High School Diploma/GED – 24.3% have a college degree and 7.2% have a higher degree • 51.4% of families have a child under 18 at home • 4.2% of workers take public transit (but 12.5% carpool) • 18.6% of households have incomes under $25k • Exactly half of all households are renters (the other half are owners) 4

## Districting Process and
Public Input 17
* * *
## Council District Mapping Process
1. 1 st round of Public Meetings: May-Early June 2015 – Purpose to get input on communities of interest and understand the issues here in Anaheim – Next meeting to be held in West Anaheim (LOCATION IF POSS) 2. Draft proposals released: Early July 2015 – Options based on public feedback/testimony – All proposals submitted by members of the public also available 3. 2 nd Round of Public Meetings: Throughout July 2015 – Debate draft proposals and make changes as needed based on feedback/testimony – Commission may make a recommendation to the Council on what plan(s) to adopt 4. Council Consideration and Approval – Council must hold at least three public hearings 5. First election in new districts 18
* * *
## Public Input is Vital
• Define your “community of interest” – To be drawn into a map, we need geographic boundaries of the community • Share your opinions about proposed district lines • Draw your own idea of where proposed lines might go 19
* * *
## Additional Opportunities for Input
• Speak during public comment periods • Send a letter or an email • Draw your own district: – Draw your neighborhood or community of interest on the maps here tonight • Whatever input you can provide is encouraged – Draw using the Public Participation Kits • Available on www.anaheim.net/districts/ as an interactive Excel spreadsheet or printed tonight 20
* * *
## We Want to Hear from You!
For more information, please visit: www.anaheim.net/districts/ E-mail: DistrictCommittee@anaheim.net Telephone: (714) 765-5166 Mail: Office of the City Clerk Attn: District Mapping City of Anaheim

## _200 S. Anaheim Blvd._
Anaheim, CA 92805
* * *
TEL: 714.765.5166 FAX: 714.765.4105 Date: May 22, 2015 To: Advisory Committee on Electoral Districts From: Linda N. Andal, City Clerk Subject: Item No. 4 – Remote Locations On May 12, 2015, the Advisory Committee on Electoral Districts (Committee) approved various meeting dates and spoke about the importance of holding meetings in the community, directing staff to procure meeting locations in West Anaheim (June 4 meeting) and South Anaheim (July 8 meeting). As such, the June 4 meeting is scheduled at the Brookhurst Community Center located at
* * *
## _2271 West Crescent Avenue. The July 8 meeting is scheduled at the Ponderosa Family_
Resource Center, located at 100 South Haster; both meetings are scheduled to begin at 6:30
* * *
p.m. In addition, staff was able to secure the East Anaheim Community Center, located at
* * *
## _8201 East Santa Ana Canyon Road, for the Committee’s June 9 meeting. Therefore, if the_
Committee wishes to hold the June 9 meeting offsite, East Anaheim is recommended; this
* * *
will ensure all current neighborhood districts have been attended by the Committee to afford greater community involvement during the first phase of the drawing process. It is important to note that although north Anaheim is not an identified “neighborhood council area,” staff recognizes the distance between the northern border and East Anaheim. As such, staff attempted to secure a meeting location at Miraloma Resource Center and Rio Vista Elementary, however parking at the Miraloma Resource Center was limited in the evening and Rio Vista Elementary could not be secured at this time. All offsite Committee meetings will be audio-taped and made available on the Districting webpage within 48 hours. Spanish interpretation services will be available, with other languages available upon request. Outreach to inform the communities in these areas, as well as throughout Anaheim, will continue to ensure interested residents are made aware of the meetings and encouraged to attend and participate. A map depicting the proposed meeting locations is attached as well as the meeting calendar, to date. revised 5-22
* * *

## ADVISORY COMMITTEE ON ELECTORAL DISTRICTS MINUTES
TUESDAY, MAY 12, 2015 6:30 P.M. Anaheim City Council Chambers Committee Members Present: Hon. James Jackman, Ret.; Hon. Nancy Wieben Stock, Ret.; Hon. Stephen Sundvold, Ret.; Hon. Thomas Thrasher, Ret.; Hon. Edward Wallin, Ret. Staff Present: City Clerk Linda Andal, Outside Counsel Ben De Mayo, Consultant Justin Levitt. 1. Call meeting to order: The meeting of the Advisory Co mmittee on Electoral Districts (ACED) was called to order at 6:41pm by City Clerk Linda Andal. The membe rs of the committee and staff introduced themselves with brief comments. City Clerk Linda Andal reviewed housekeeping items for the meeting as follows: the City Clerk will fa cilitate the meeting until the Chair is selected under Agenda Item No. 3, seating at the dais i s currently alphabetical and will change at future meetings based on the outcome of Agenda Item No. 3, me etings held in the chambers will be video-taped and available online within 48 hours of each meeting, all agendas and back-up material will be available online and at th e City Clerk’s office at least 72 hours prior to each meeting, microphones should be turned on when speaking and off when not speaking, Spanish interpretatio n will be available at every committee meeting with other language interpreters available upon 48 hour prior request to the City Clerk’s office. 2. Public Comments (3 minutes – all agenda items except Item No. 6, District Presentation): City Clerk Linda Andal explained sp eaker cards would be used at each meeting, though not mandatory, rather as a tool to help facilitate the meeting and create a list of interested persons for future outreach. Vic Real, Anaheim resident, indicate d he had never felt unrepresented and was always involved in the City, including serving on the past election committee. He acknowledged the large task in front of the committee and was looking forward to citizens voting and exerting democracy. Brian Chuchua thanked t he committee for being here, congratulated them on accepting the challenging work, and expressed his disappointment that the audience was not full. Greg Diamo nd, Brea resident, directed the committee’s attention to the 2011 hearings of the California Redistrict ing Commission, the extensive archives of their meetings, and expressed his hope that this committee would emulate that commission. Mr. Diamond questioned whether the City would allow members of the public to use freely available software to engage in th eir own redistricting and encouraged the use of such technology, specifically limiting by census blo ck. He also directed the committee’s attention to election law cases a nd the concepts of “packing” and “cracking,” each of which he indicated was bad for minorities. ITEM NO. 05
* * *
Regular Meeting of the Advisory Committee on Electoral Districts May 12, 2015 Page 2 of 5
* * *
Dr. Patricia Adelekan, Anaheim resident, thanked the committee for their time and contribution to get this job done. She questioned how problems could be solved if people were not at the table. She encouraged people at home to participate in the decisions to be made, and then no one could complain if they do not take responsibility now. Mariana Rivera (through a Spanish interpreter) thanked the committee and expressed appreciation on behalf of the community. Ms. Rivera remarked she lived in the Guinida area for about 12 years and started getting involved about 6 years ago to help her community. She spoke about issues she has seen such as poverty, parents working three jobs, and kids turning to gangs. She expressed her support for district elections as a way to help communities and families receive equally divided resources. Gloria Ma’ae, Anaheim resident and former member of Anaheim’s Citizens Advisory Committee on Elections and Community Involvement, expressed her thanks to the committee for serving, her gratitude for looking at different districting options, encouraged the committee to be fair and balanced, and was looking forward to the process. 3. Elect Chair and Co-Chair: Judge Sundvold nominated Justice Edward Wallin to Chair, seconded by Judge Stock. With no other nominations for Chair, City Clerk Andal called for a vote. Approved Vote: 5-0. Justice Edward Wallin was appointed Chair. Chairman Wallin nominated Stephen Sundvold for Vice Chair, seconded by Judge Stock. With no other nominations for Vice Chair, Chairman Wallin called for a vote. Approved Vote: 4-0-1. AYES4 (Chairman Wallin and Judges Jackman, Stock, and Thrasher). NOES – 0. ABSTENTION – 1 (Judge Sundvold). Judge Stephen Sundvold was appointed Vice Chair. 4. Brown Act Presentation: Prior to the presentation, City Attorney Michael Houston provided a brief description on the creation of the committee pursuant to a settlement agreement. Mr. Houston then presented a PowerPoint presentation of the Ralph M. Brown Act, as applicable to public meetings of legislative bodies, including this committee. 5. Receive and File memo from City Attorney regarding Legal Issues and Parliamentary Procedures: Judge Jackman moved to approve Item No. 5, seconded by Judge Thrasher. Approved Vote: 5-0. 6. Council District Presentation: Demographic consultant, Justin Levitt, gave a presentation on council districts including the history of how the City arrived at this process through voter approval of Measures L & M at the November 2014 election. Mr. Levitt described various Federal and State regulations, laws, and criteria that affect the establishment of districts, indicating that beyond complying with the federal and state mandates the committee could determine which criteria are most important to them. He explained several breakdowns of city demographics based on the 2010 Census data including total population, voting age population, Hispanic/non-Hispanic White/Asian citizen voting age population, education,
* * *
Regular Meeting of the Advisory Committee on Electoral Districts May 12, 2015 Page 3 of 5 family size, transportation needs, income level, language, and home-ownership data; however noting that all this data is no substitute for members of the public telling the committee what their communities are and what they mean to them. Mr. Levitt then discussed the overall districting process expressing the importance of public input during the first round of public meetings. This first round, he explained, would get communities of interest together to discuss and understand the process and issues in Anaheim, which could result in the creation of at least 2-3 draft proposals based on public feedback and testimony. A second round of public meetings would be held for debate on the draft proposals prior to the committee making their final recommendation to the City Council. He shared that the Committee has the option of presenting several plans to Council in their final recommendation. Thereafter, the City Council will hold at least three public hearings, advising that changes to the maps could still be made. The final map approved by the City Council would be used in the November 2016 election. Mr. Levitt concluded his presentation by emphasizing that public input was vital and this process would allow residents to define their community of interest by geographic boundaries and to share their opinions about proposed district lines. a. Public Comment on Council District Presentation, only (3 minutes): Greg Diamond questioned whether the units on the public participation maps could be subdivided into smaller areas and how to obtain the population of the subdivisions and encouraged the committee to be on guard of existing and potential candidate locations being tied into other presented data and to avoid snaking districts. Mr. Levitt responded that each unit on the map consisted of one to several hundred blocks, including approximately 1,000 people, remarking that the block file can be made available upon request. Vic Real requested clarification on the existing dash lines on the maps as being the current Neighborhood District Council boundaries. Mr. Levitt confirmed the purple lines on the displayed map indicated current Neighborhood District Council boundaries with the orange lines representing school districts within the city. Benita Gagne, Anaheim Republican Assembly President, reported they had a district boundary drawing contest at the WAND BBQ and submitted a representation of 11 contestant entries. She questioned whether the units on the public participation maps were contiguous with current voting precincts and if not, would it cause problems for the Registrar of Voters. Mr. Levitt advised that after the City Council approves the final maps, the final step would be to work with the Orange County Registrar of Voters to determine the precincts based on the new district boundaries.
* * *
Regular Meeting of the Advisory Committee on Electoral Districts May 12, 2015 Page 4 of 5 Dr. Patricia Adelekan expressed her view that public input is very important and inquired about the method of getting the word out to the community as many are not on internet and whether there is a plan to transport people to the committee meetings. Ms. Andal advised that a community outreach plan would be presented following public comments which would address Dr. Adelekan’s comments. Responding to the question of reaching people who were unable to make it to the meetings, Ms. Andal referenced an upcoming item on the agenda which allowed the committee members to schedule meetings in the communities, not just City Council Chambers. Alejandra Montseñor, questioned how the committee is taking input from communities and going through the provided feedback/testimonies. Chairman Wallin and Mr. De Mayo provided clarifying remarks about the process that the committee will get a full analysis from the demographer as well as all maps submitted by the public. The committee will then make suggestions for changes to the maps over the course of several meetings and present a preferred option with City Council also receiving the same data and holding at least three public hearings in accordance with State law before adopting the final maps. 7. Presentation of Community Outreach Plan: City Clerk Linda Andal presented the community outreach plan for this districting process and went through a number of efforts for the first meeting of the committee and current efforts underway for future meetings. Highlighted in the presentation was the e-Postcard, a grass roots effort where identified community groups and leaders were contacted and asked to forward to their membership, Fast Facts, a one page document with the primary information about the committee and the districting process; both documents were provided in English and Spanish with other languages available upon request. Ms. Andal also reviewed the dedicated webpage, www.anaheim.net/districts, through which the website and associated documents would available in English, Spanish, Chinese, Vietnamese, and Korean. Chairman Wallin added that as this was the first time districts are being drawn in Anaheim rather than merely adjusting district lines, the task is more challenging. Mr. Levitt indicated that the impact of this project is not just in the current time but also into the future as in 2021, the districts drawn through this process would be used as a base for potential changes as the result of the 2020 Federal Census. 8. Committee meeting calendar: The committee discussed their availability on several dates in May, June, and July and directed staff to procure locations, other than the Council Chambers, for certain meetings. Judge Thrasher moved to approve the following dates and locations for future committee meetings, all to begin at 6:30 p.m.: Wednesday, May 27 – Council Chambers Thursday, June 4 – West Anaheim location Tuesday, June 9 – Council Chambers Wednesday, July 1 – Council Chambers
* * *
Regular Meeting of the Advisory Committee on Electoral Districts May 12, 2015 Page 5 of 5 Wednesday, July 8 – South Anaheim location
* * *
Seconded by Chairman Wallin. Approved Vote: 5-0.
* * *
9. Committee Comments / Staff Comments: Chairman Wallin thanked everyone for being good citizens by attending and participating in the meeting. 10. Adjourn meeting: Chairman Wallin adjourned the ACED meeting at 8:32pm. Respectfully submitted,
* * *
Linda N. Andal, CMC City Clerk

LỊCH TRÌNH HỌP CÁC THÀNH VIÊN H ỘI ĐỒNG
* * *
Thứ Tư, 1 Tháng Bảy, 2015 Hon. Edward Wallin, Ret., Ch ủ Tịch 6:30 chiều Hon. Stephen Sundvold, Ret., Phó Ch ủ Tịch Phòng Họp Hội Đồng, Tòa Thị Sảnh Thành Phố Anaheim Hon. James Jackman, Ret.
* * *
## _200 S. Anaheim Blvd. Anaheim 92805 Hon. Nancy Wieben Stock, Ret._
Hon. Thomas Thrasher, Ret.
* * *
Triệu Tập Họp:
* * *
Ý Kiến của Cộng Đồng (3 phúttất cả các mục của lịch trình).
* * *
1. Thảo luận và trình bày bản thảo đường biên địa hạt Hội Đồng Thành Phố với hướng dẫn khả thi cho ban điều hành.
* * *
2. Chấp thuận lịch họp Hội Đồng.
* * *
3. Chấp thuận biên bản họp ngày 4 tháng Sáu và 9 tháng Sáu, 2015 của Hội Đồng Cố Vấn về Địa Hạt Bẩu Cử.
* * *
4. Các Ý Kiến của Hội Đồng / Ý Kiến của Ban điều hành
* * *
Kết thúc họp. Buổi họp thường lệ tiếp theo được hoạch định vào ngày 8 tháng Bảy, 2015 lúc 6:30 chiều ở Trung Tâm Ponderosa Resource Family, 2100 S. Haster St., Anaheim.
* * *
** Viên chức nhân khẩu học của thành phố sẽ có mặt ở nơi họp trước một tiếng đồng hồ và ngay sau buổi họp để cung cấp trợ giúp thực hành trên mạng với các dụng cụ bản đồ.
* * *
*****
* * *
Tất cả các mục của lịch trình và các tài liệu hỗ trợ đều có sẵn sàng để xem xét lại tại Văn Phòng Thư Ký Thành Phố, và tại http://www.anaheim.net/article.asp?id=5419. Bất cứ văn bản hay tài liệu nào cung cấp đa số của Hội Đồng về bất cứ mục nào trong lịch trình này (ngoài các văn bản được pháp lý miễn trừ tiết lộ ra công cộng) đều phải có sẵn sàng cho công chúng xem xét ở Văn Phòng Thư Ký Thành Phố, tọa lạc tại 200 S. Anaheim Blvd., Lầu 2, Anaheim, CA 92805 trong giờ hành chánh bình thường.
* * *
Bất cứ ai cần có sự cải biến hoặc làm cho thích nghi với điều kiện khuyết tật, kể cả những sự trợ giúp hay các dịch vụ bổ túc thêm, để có thể tham gia vào buổi họp cộng đồng, đều có thể yêu cầu một sự trợ giúp hay các dịch vụ cải biến thích nghi như vậy bằng cách liên lạc với Văn Phòng Thư Ký Thành Phố ở 200 South Anaheim Boulevard, Anaheim, California, hoặc điện thoại số (714) 765-5166, không trễ quá 10 giờ sáng ngày hôm trước của buổi họp theo lịch trình. Tùy theo yêu cầu, lịch trình này sẽ được làm sẵn sàng với hình thức thay đổi thích hợp với những người khuyết tật, theo như đòi hỏi của Chương 202 của Đạo Luật Người Mỹ Khuyết Tật, năm 1990.
* * *
DỊCH VỤ THỐNG DỊCH: dịch vụ thông dịch tiếng Tây Ban Nha được cung cấp cho các buổi họp Hội Đồng Cố Vấn. Sự Thông Dịch Đồng Thời được cung cấp qua việc xử dụng máy nghe tai, và sự thông dịch tiếp liền nhau (Tây Ban Nha –sang- Anh Ngữ) cũng có sẵn sàng cho những ai muốn truyền đạt với Hội Đồng bằng cách nói lên thỉnh nguyện của mình trước bục sân khấu. Không bắt buộc phải xử dụng thông dịch viên do thành phố cung cấp, quý vị có thể tự nhiên xử dụng các người thông dịch riêng cho mình. Do có nhiều tiếng địa phương và tiếng đặc biệt của các vùng, Thành phố không thể bảo đảm rằng các thông dịch viên sẽ dịch theo một tiếng địa phương hay của một vùng nào nhất định, và không chịu bất cứ một trách nhiệm pháp lý nào với các kiện cáo do các dịch vụ như vậy gây ra. Để có được dịch vụ thông dịch với các ngôn ngữ khác, xin liên lạc với văn phòng của Thư Ký Thành Phố, không trễ quá 48 tiếng đồng hồ trước ngày họp theo lịch trình.
* * *
TUYÊN BỐ YẾT THỊ: Vào ngày 26 tháng Sáu, 2015, một bản sao đúng thật và chính xác của lịch trình này được đưa ra yết thị tại quầy phía ngoài Tòa Thị Sảnh Thành Phố, 200 S. Anaheim Blvd.

Date: July 1, 2015

To: Advisory Committee on Electoral Districts
* * *
From: Linda N. Andal, City Clerk
* * *
Subject: Item No. 1 – Draft City Council Boundaries
* * *
At the June 9, 2015 meeting, the Advisory Committee on Electoral Districts (Committee) directed the city’s demographer, Justin Levitt, to develop draft City Council district boundary maps based on the legal criteria outlined in past meetings, including consideration of communities of interest, communities established by school and special district boundaries and land use planning areas. Additionally, the Committee requested the proposed map(s) consider multiple districts bordering the Resort District as well as boundary consideration around the area of the Santa Ana River and the 91 freeway. Mr. Levitt, has prepared three (3) draft maps for the Committee’s consideration, which will be made available online, at the City Clerk’s office and various city facilities, such as libraries and community centers. The drafts are intended for discussion purposes only; the demographer is not recommending approval on any proposal. Mr. Levitt has prepared and will present a demographic analysis of the three draft proposals. The City Clerk has received thirteen (13) draft proposals for City Council boundaries from various individuals and groups, which are attached to this staff report and will be made available in both electronic and paper form, for use during public comments by the original submitter or interested persons. As such, Mr. Levitt has prepared a demographic analysis on each public submittal. Upon receipt of each public submission, the City Clerk posted each map as originally submitted (www.anaheim.net/districts). Mr. Levitt reviewed each map and attempted to make contact with each submitter to verify the data was accurately reflected and the boundaries correctly drawn. The final version of each submittal that accompanies this staff report reflects the intent of the submitter. The city continues to encourage residents to submit draft boundary proposals, revisions to submitted maps or offer comments on any maps. The city’s demographer will continue to review all submissions and make revisions as necessary, based on Committee direction and community input. To allow adequate time for the demographer to review submissions, develop (revised) maps, and Committee discussion, staff encourages the public to submit maps by July 31, 2015.
* * *

## PROPOSED DISTRICTS FOR ADVISORY COMMITTEE ON ELECTORIAL DISTRICTS
PROPOSED BY RONALD BENGOCHEA (LIFETIME ANAHEIM RESIDENT) 6‐09‐15 Listed below is my proposal for designations for the 6 Electorial Districts. This proposal is based upon my living in Anaheim, born & raised & also working for the City of Anaheim Utilities Dept. for 35+ years. I also attended every meeting of the Advisory committee to bring forward a Proposition to be placed on the ballot in 2014 for District Election of Council Members by the residents. (I missed a total of 2 of these meetings). The Major concern by 80% or more comments by the public stated “We have no repre sentation for our community on the City Council” My proposal, I believe meets all the concerns voiced at the various meetings. DISTRICRT #1 (North East District) DISTRICT #2(South East District) Tustin Ave/East to end of City Limits Tustin Ave/East to end of City Limits. Nort h of Lincoln Ave/Nohl Ranch Rd. South of Lincoln Ave./Nohl Ranch Rd. Then North of Canyon Rim Rd. Then South of Canyon Rim Rd. DISTRICT #3 (North Central District) DISTRICT #4 (South Central District) Tustin Ave West to Euclid St. Tustin Ave West to Euclid St. North of Lincoln Ave. South of Lincoln Ave. DISTRICT #5 (North West District DISTRICT #5 (South West District) West of Euclid St./North of Lincoln West of Euclid St./South of Lincoln To end of City Limits To end of City Limits
* * *
I believe this proposal represents the concerns & desires of all Anaheim residents and will meet most of the dem ographics concerns as well. The will bring simplicity for the residents as far as recognizing which their represented district location will be. Respectfully, Ronald Bengochea
* * *
Submitted by Chuchua, Brian and Diamond, Greg
* * *
1 Linda Andal From: Greg Diamond Sent: Wednesday, June 24, 2015 4:30 PM To: District Committee Cc: Brian Chuchua; Greg Diamond Subject: Brian Chuchua districting submission: Map 2 (Euclid border) Attachments: Chuchua Assignments for Map #2 (Euclid Border).xls; Chuchua Stats & Map #2 (Euclid Border).pdf This submission by Brian Chuchua, with technical assistance by Greg Diamond, contains two attachments:
* * *
(1) Spreadsheet containing Assignments, Balance Statistics, and an extra tab with Notes Regarding Map Features
* * *
(2) Separate PDF containing repeat of Balance Statistics (without color) and a map colored by District and Census Block Group.
* * *
This map was completed without obtaining any information regarding partisanship and ignores the residency of prospective candidates. It is driven primarily by the demands of geography, the need for equal population and adherence to legal requirements, and respect for communities of interest.
* * *
The main intent of this map is to show that a simple, intuitive, non-partisan map with contiguous, compact districts of (after some minor splitting of census blocks) exactly equal population is absolutely possible for Anaheim. No map that lacks those characteristics (except possibly for some tolerance regarding exactly equal population) should be considered acceptable.

NOTES ON CHUCHUA MAP #2 (EUCLID BORDER) ~~ DONE WITHOUT REFERENCE TO PARTISANSHIP OR RESIDENCY 1. This map's name derives from the fact that it generally uses Euclid Avenue to divide District 2 from Districts 3 and 4. 2. District 1 (in orange, primarily the Southwest Anaheim peninsula) is both logically sited and only 11 residents short of the target population. 3. District 1 is a coherent area west of Anaheim Island and not close to I-5. Switching CBGs 31 & 35 would require dividing CBG 35 for balance. 4. It should be readily possible, if desired, to move 11 residents from the far south of CBG (Census Blog Group) 29 to perfect the balance. 5. District 6 (Anaheim Hills roughly east of Tustin, in blue) barely appears on the attached map, but includes everything east of District 5. 6. It should be readily possible to move 164 residents from westernmost District 6 (CBG 171 or 174) into District 5 to perfect the balance. 7. The eastern border of District 2 (West Anaheim, in green) is mostly Euclid Ave., a natural border (with almost exactly 1/3 of the city west of it.) 8. The western border of District 2 is easily understood, ending at the Anaheim Island, then briefly at Dale, then mostly at Magnolia (+CBG 29) 9. It should be readily possible to move 292 residents from the far west of CBGs 49 and 64 (in District 3) into District 2 to perfect the balance. 10. The northern border of District 4 (primarily South Anaheim, in red) is Ball Rd. to its east and the five CBGs bordering Ball Rd., to its west. 11. The eastern border of District 4 is Euclid Ave; the southern and western borders are the city limits (with the bottom tail of CBG 163 being optional). 12. It should be readily possible to move 343 residents into District 3 and 144 into District 5 from CBG 123 in District 4 to perfect the balance. 13. District 3 (primarily North and Central Anaheim in purple) has relatively clear borders, mostly Euclid to East and Vermont to the border. 14. The eastern border of District 3 (i.e., the western border of District 5) generally follows East St. This line could continue through CBGs 132 and 137.) 15. The northern border of District 5 (primarily Northeast Anaheim, in yellow) follows the City limits; the eastern borders District 6. 16. The southern border of District 5 is along Ball Rd (The tail of CBG 163 is easily moved into District 4.) The western border mostly follows East St. 17. With 51.3% to 51.6% Latino CVAP, District 3 is a "majority-minority" district under the VRA. 18. Districts 4 and 5 are plurality Latino districts: the former by 7.0% to 8.5% (Latino CVAP 42.1% to 42.9%) and the latter by 7.3% to 7.8% (LCVAP ~45%) 19. District 6 is majority white. Districts 1 and 2 are closely divided between White and Latino, both with substantial Asian populations. 20. District 2 contains almost all of Little Arabia (as much as is possible, given the limitations of District 1.) 21. District 3 contains all of Central Anaheim's historic Colony District along with adjacent pre-war housing districts of similar character north and west. 22. District 4 contains all of the Resort District, although it should be noted that that district itself is depopulated, and areas closest to Garden Grove. 23. District 5 contains the eastern portion of Central Anaheim, the area around State College and the 57, and the Anaheim Canyon.
* * *
Submitted by Dresser, Michael

From: James Duron Sent: Monday, June 01, 2015 6:28:50 PM (UTC-08:00) Pacific Time (US & Canada) To: District Committee Subject: A Single community-based District Proposal Your Honors, I submit to you a district parcel proposal of my distinctive neighborhood. In my first attempt to outline my neighborhood, much to my surprise, that I was able to meet the criteria in fairness and balance reflecting the U.S. Census racial data, and all within the confines of existing natural boundaries. Also maintaining a population count well within the 5% tolerance. I do sincerely hope you give my proposal an honest appraisal. Thank you all for your civic efforts. Regards, James R. Duron

Comments: The attache d plan is an attempt to stick with the spirit of the law, to create as compact districts of even size as possible, and to use obvious physical barriers that separate communities to divide districts, and from there to see how the demographics of each district broke down. * All six districts in this plan are close in population, the largest deviation from the average is 888 individuals (1.6%). * This plan uses I-5 as a physical dividing line between districts, where practical, which only one district spanning the freeway. * The district that spans I-5 includes Disneyland, the Platinum Triangle, Angel Stadium, and the Honda Center. The residents living in these areas will have similar interests despite living on opposite sides of the 5. * This plan keeps the core of the Colony in a single district. * This plan keeps Little Arabia together in a single district. * This plan has half of the districts with a majority Hispanic population, two of which have Hispanic super-majorities, which is consistent with the demographics of Anaheim. This plan shows that a non-gerrymandered district map is possible to create, that would be legal and fairly represent the interests of Anaheim residents.
* * *

Submitted by LULAC, Santa Ana Montez, Arturo & Hernandez, Zeke
* * *
## June 23, 2015
Advisory Committee on Electoral Districts City of Anaheim
* * *
## _200 South Anaheim Boulevard_
Anaheim, California 92805
* * *
Hon. Chairman Wallin and Hon. Committee Members:
* * *
The Santa Ana League of United Latin American Citizens Council #147 (LULAC) is submitting two maps for Anaheim City Council by-district elections for your consideration. The maps, which are also supported by California LULAC, were drawn by Mr. Arturo Montez. 1
* * *
These two plans, hereafter referred to as LULAC Map #1 and LULAC Map #2, comply with the U.S. Constitutional and Federal Voting Rights Act (VRA) districting mandates. They also represent scenarios which uphold the integrity of the city’s protected class of communities and do not maliciously divide communities of interest within the city of Anaheim.
* * *
Further, we ask that the LULAC map submitted June 19 via email by Mr. Arturo Montez not be considered. This map was submitted as a draft to the City Council’s demographer to verify statistics for compliance with the Federal Voting Rights Act. The new LULAC Map #1 is that preliminary map’s final edit, adjusted for VRA compliance. LULAC Map #1 features two districts with over 50% Latino Citizen Voting Age Population, which is a threshold needed for examination of whether a district is a minority-majority district for the purposes of the VRA review.
* * *
LULAC believes any plan for Anaheim City council must have at least two Latino majority districts. However LULAC Map #2 is a plan that demonstrates to the Advisory Committee on Electoral Districts that three geographically compact districts can be created with over 50% Latino Citizen Voting Age Population. We ask that this plan be examined as well.
* * *
We fully understand the responsibilities, commitments, and the sacrifices members of the Advisory Committee on Electoral Districts have undertaken in accepting a role in this reform of the electoral process in the City of Anaheim. Mr. Montez and I have diligently worked as community volunteers on drawing redistricting maps since post-1980 U.S. Census results and continue to do so today – per the changes called for under the California Voting Rights Act.
* * *
As we worked through the process, LULAC was confronted with and placed a major and considerable amount of time with respect to the massive man-made construction features within
* * *
## We thank the Mexican American Legal Defense and Educational Fund (MALDEF) for providing technical support
to Mr. Montez as he crafted these plans.
* * *
the city boundaries; in particular the four major state freeways (5, 55, 57, and 91) that crisscross the city. In providing a quick glimpse to local history, there was a time when city policy-makers engineered transit freeways to divide communities. Some folks viewed this as a form of gentrification. LULAC believes that these concrete freeways have only cemented the strong bonds and ties of neighborhoods residents on both sides of multi-lane pathways for vehicular travel – especially as to Anaheim's Latino community.
* * *
LULAC wishes to recognize the tireless efforts and determination of the average, everyday individuals who stepped forward in seeking a solution to the process as it is today. They took a bold step when they filed their concerns with the courts. We are particularly mindful that in the November 2014 elections, the prevailing electorate agreed with these three individuals. A great many Anaheim residents should be grateful to this trio of citizens for a "job well done".
* * *
In conclusion, LULAC (through its state organization and local chapter) respectfully submits to the Advisory Committee on Electoral DistrictsLULAC Map #1 and LULAC Map #2 for your careful consideration as you work to provide the City of Anaheim the best possible by-district election reform in this process.
* * *
Again, we present our maps for your consideration, and do pray that this esteemed body of Anaheim residents will rely on your own experiences, expertise, and wisdom to present the best possible recommendations based on your findings, in your final report to the Anaheim City Council.
* * *
Respectfully Submitted,
* * *
/s/ Arturo Montez Public Policy Director Santa Ana LULAC #147 League of United Latin American Citizens
* * *
/s/Zeke Hernandez Executive Board Member, California LULAC and President, Santa Ana LULAC #147
* * *

* * *
## June 23, 2015
Advisory Committee on Electoral Districts City of Anaheim
* * *
## _200 South Anaheim Boulevard_
Anaheim, California 92805
* * *
Hon. Chairman Wallin and Hon. Committee Members:
* * *
The Santa Ana League of United Latin American Citizens Council #147 (LULAC) is submitting two maps for Anaheim City Council by-district elections for your consideration. The maps, which are also supported by California LULAC, were drawn by Mr. Arturo Montez. 1
* * *
These two plans, hereafter referred to as LULAC Map #1 and LULAC Map #2, comply with the U.S. Constitutional and Federal Voting Rights Act (VRA) districting mandates. They also represent scenarios which uphold the integrity of the city’s protected class of communities and do not maliciously divide communities of interest within the city of Anaheim.
* * *
Further, we ask that the LULAC map submitted June 19 via email by Mr. Arturo Montez not be considered. This map was submitted as a draft to the City Council’s demographer to verify statistics for compliance with the Federal Voting Rights Act. The new LULAC Map #1 is that preliminary map’s final edit, adjusted for VRA compliance. LULAC Map #1 features two districts with over 50% Latino Citizen Voting Age Population, which is a threshold needed for examination of whether a district is a minority-majority district for the purposes of the VRA review.
* * *
LULAC believes any plan for Anaheim City council must have at least two Latino majority districts. However LULAC Map #2 is a plan that demonstrates to the Advisory Committee on Electoral Districts that three geographically compact districts can be created with over 50% Latino Citizen Voting Age Population. We ask that this plan be examined as well.
* * *
We fully understand the responsibilities, commitments, and the sacrifices members of the Advisory Committee on Electoral Districts have undertaken in accepting a role in this reform of the electoral process in the City of Anaheim. Mr. Montez and I have diligently worked as community volunteers on drawing redistricting maps since post-1980 U.S. Census results and continue to do so today – per the changes called for under the California Voting Rights Act.
* * *
As we worked through the process, LULAC was confronted with and placed a major and considerable amount of time with respect to the massive man-made construction features within
* * *
## We thank the Mexican American Legal Defense and Educational Fund (MALDEF) for providing technical support
to Mr. Montez as he crafted these plans.
* * *
the city boundaries; in particular the four major state freeways (5, 55, 57, and 91) that crisscross the city. In providing a quick glimpse to local history, there was a time when city policy-makers engineered transit freeways to divide communities. Some folks viewed this as a form of gentrification. LULAC believes that these concrete freeways have only cemented the strong bonds and ties of neighborhoods residents on both sides of multi-lane pathways for vehicular travel – especially as to Anaheim's Latino community.
* * *
LULAC wishes to recognize the tireless efforts and determination of the average, everyday individuals who stepped forward in seeking a solution to the process as it is today. They took a bold step when they filed their concerns with the courts. We are particularly mindful that in the November 2014 elections, the prevailing electorate agreed with these three individuals. A great many Anaheim residents should be grateful to this trio of citizens for a "job well done".
* * *
In conclusion, LULAC (through its state organization and local chapter) respectfully submits to the Advisory Committee on Electoral DistrictsLULAC Map #1 and LULAC Map #2 for your careful consideration as you work to provide the City of Anaheim the best possible by-district election reform in this process.
* * *
Again, we present our maps for your consideration, and do pray that this esteemed body of Anaheim residents will rely on your own experiences, expertise, and wisdom to present the best possible recommendations based on your findings, in your final report to the Anaheim City Council.
* * *
Respectfully Submitted,
* * *
/s/ Arturo Montez Public Policy Director Santa Ana LULAC #147 League of United Latin American Citizens
* * *
/s/Zeke Hernandez Executive Board Member, California LULAC and President, Santa Ana LULAC #147

Comments: This Anaheim City Council District proposal is meant to ensure the m ajor landmarks in the city are spread among as many of the Council Districts as possible. Great care was also taken to ensure neighborhoods were kept together, particularly the Colony Historic District. All district boundaries stay along main arterial streets and have a total deviation of 3.4%. District 1: Located in the far west of Anaheim, major landmarks are Twila Reid Park, Adventure City, and Brookhurst Community Center. District 2: Primarily located in west/central Anaheim, major landmarks include Disneyland, Convention Center, Downtown Disney and Tiger Woods Learning Center. This district is meant to also include Little Arabia by going around the "county island" to include the Magnolia corridor. District 3: Based in Southeast Anaheim, major landmarks include Gardenwalk, Angels Stadium, Honda Center and ARTIC. This district is designed to include many southern working class neighborhoods as well as keeping the Platinum Triangle whole. District 4: A north/central based seat, this district is meant to encompass the Colony Historic District. Major landmarks include Anaheim Packing House, City Hall and Civic Center Promenade and Pearson Park. In addition to the Colony, other working class neighborhoods surrounding the Colony are included. District 5: This district is meant to encompass the working class neighborhoods in Northeast Anaheim. Major landmarks include The Canyon Business District, Anaheim Coves and La Palma Park. District 6: This district contains the Anaheim Hills portion of the city. Major landmarks are the Santa Ana River Lakes, Yorba Regional Park and Oak Canyon Nature Center.
* * *

From: Linda N. Andal, City Clerk
* * *
Subject: Item No. 2 – Approve Meeting Calendar
* * *
At the June 9, 2015 Advisory Committee on Electoral Districts meeting, the Committee provided additional public meetings dates through September 2015 and directed staff to procure meeting locations in West Anaheim (August 26) and South Anaheim (September 8). As such, it is recommended that the Committee formally adopt the attached meeting calendar setting forth the following public meetings of the Committee; all meetings will continue to commence at 6:30 p.m.: August 19, City Hall Council Chambers; August 26, Western High School, 501 S. Western Avenue, Cafeteria; September 8, 1765 Cerritos Avenue, Room 208; and September 14, City Hall Council Chambers. A map depicting proposed and past meeting locations is attached as well as an updated calendar, which has also been posted online and available at various city facilities, such as libraries and community centers. In addition to the scheduled meetings, the City Clerk and city’s demographer will attend the regularly scheduled Neighborhood Council Meetings on July 15 (West District, West Anaheim Youth Center), July 16 (East District, Miraloma Park Family Resource Center), July 22 (Central District, Downtown Community Center), and July 23 (South District, Paul Revere Elementary School), beginning at 7:00 p.m. In our continual effort towards education, public engagement and participation about the districting process, staff will share the current draft maps during these neighborhood meetings and answer questions. All meetings of the Committee are recorded and made available on the Districting webpage and ACTV 3. Spanish interpretation services are available at each meeting, including the Neighborhood Council meetings, with other languages available upon request.
* * *
